# Architecture Q&A: Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline

**Repository:** hashicorp/terraform
**Task Type:** Architecture Q&A (investigation only — no code changes)

## Background

Terraform's `terraform plan` command builds a dependency graph of all resources in the configuration, resolves providers, and computes the diff between desired state and current state. This process involves multiple layers: CLI command parsing, backend operation execution, graph construction via a series of transformers, concurrent graph walking, and provider plugin communication for diff computation.

## Questions

Answer ALL of the following questions about Terraform's plan execution pipeline:

### Q1: Command to Context

When a user runs `terraform plan`, how does the CLI command reach the core planning logic? Specifically:
- How does `PlanCommand.Run()` in `internal/command/plan.go` delegate to the backend?
- How does the backend create and invoke `terraform.Context.Plan()`?
- What are the key fields of `PlanOpts` that control plan behavior (mode, targets, force-replace)?

### Q2: Graph Construction Pipeline

How does `PlanGraphBuilder` construct the dependency graph for a plan operation?
- What is the role of the `Steps()` method and how does the sequence of `GraphTransformer` stages build the graph?
- Specifically, what do `ConfigTransformer`, `ReferenceTransformer`, and `AttachStateTransformer` each contribute?
- How does `ReferenceTransformer` analyze node references to add dependency edges between resources?

### Q3: Provider Resolution and Configuration

How are providers resolved, initialized, and configured during the plan walk?
- How does `EvalContext.InitProvider()` instantiate a provider plugin?
- At what point in graph execution is `ConfigureProvider()` called relative to resource planning?
- What is the role of `CloseProviderTransformer` in the graph lifecycle?

### Q4: Diff Computation per Resource

For a single managed resource instance, how does Terraform compute the planned changes?
- Trace the execution path from `NodePlannableResourceInstance.Execute()` through `managedResourceExecute()`
- How does the refresh phase (`refresh()`) synchronize with remote state before planning?
- How does the `plan()` method invoke the provider's `PlanResourceChange` RPC to compute the diff?
- What determines whether a resource is marked for create, update, replace, or delete?

## Output Requirements

Write your answer to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with the following structure:

    24→	common, rawArgs := arguments.ParseView(rawArgs)

    26→

    28→	// cloud package use this; it should be removed when/if they are
    29→	// migrated to views.

    31→	c.Meta.Color = c.Meta.color
    32→
    33→	// Parse and validate flags
    34→	args, diags := arguments.ParsePlan(rawArgs)
    35→
    36→	// Instantiate the view, even if there are flag errors, so that we render
    37→	// diagnostics according to the desired view
    38→	view := views.NewPlan(args.ViewType, c.View)
    39→
    40→	if diags.HasErrors() {
    41→		view.Diagnostics(diags)
    42→		view.HelpPrompt()
    43→		return 1
    44→	}
    45→
    46→	// Check for user-supplied plugin path
    47→	var err error
    48→	if c.pluginPath, err = c.loadPluginPath(); err != nil {
    49→		diags = diags.Append(err)
    50→		view.Diagnostics(diags)
    51→		return 1
    52→	}

   674→	var diags tfdiags.Diagnostics
   675→	log.Printf("[DEBUG] Building and walking plan graph for %s", opts.Mode)
   676→
   677→	prevRunState = prevRunState.DeepCopy() // don't modify the caller's object when we process the moves
   678→	moveStmts, moveResults, moveDiags := c.prePlanFindAndApplyMoves(config, prevRunState)
   679→	diags = diags.Append(moveDiags)
   680→	if moveDiags.HasErrors() {
   681→		return nil, nil, diags
   682→	}
   683→
   684→	// If resource targeting is in effect then it might conflict with the
   685→	// move result.
   686→	diags = diags.Append(c.prePlanVerifyTargetedMoves(moveResults, opts.Targets))
   687→	if diags.HasErrors() {
   688→		// We'll return early here, because if we have any moved resource
   689→		// instances excluded by targeting then planning is likely to encounter
   690→		// strange problems that may lead to confusing error messages.
   691→		return nil, nil, diags
   692→	}
   693→
   694→	graph, walkOp, moreDiags := c.planGraph(config, prevRunState, opts)
   695→	diags = diags.Append(moreDiags)
   696→	if diags.HasErrors() {
   697→		return nil, nil, diags
   698→	}
   699→
   700→	timestamp := time.Now().UTC()
   701→	if opts.ForcePlanTimestamp != nil {
   702→		// Some tests use this to produce stable results to assert against.
   703→		timestamp = *opts.ForcePlanTimestamp
   704→	}

   706→	var externalProviderConfigs map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface
   707→	if opts != nil {
   708→		externalProviderConfigs = opts.ExternalProviders
   709→	}

    18→// PlanGraphBuilder is a GraphBuilder implementation that builds a graph for
    19→// planning and for other "plan-like" operations which don't require an
    20→// already-calculated plan as input.
    21→//
    22→// Unlike the apply graph builder, this graph builder:
    23→//
    24→//   - Makes its decisions primarily based on the given configuration, which
    25→//     represents the desired state.
    26→//
    27→//   - Ignores certain lifecycle concerns like create_before_destroy, because
    28→//     those are only important once we already know what action we're planning
    29→//     to take against a particular resource instance.
    30→type PlanGraphBuilder struct {
    31→	// Config is the configuration tree to build a plan from.
    32→	Config *configs.Config
    33→
    34→	// State is the current state
    35→	State *states.State
    36→
    37→	// RootVariableValues are the raw input values for root input variables
    38→	// given by the caller, which we'll resolve into final values as part
    39→	// of the plan walk.
    40→	RootVariableValues InputValues
    41→
    42→	// ExternalProviderConfigs are pre-initialized root module provider
    43→	// configura
... (truncated)

    19→// GraphNodeReferenceable must be implemented by any node that represents
    20→// a Terraform thing that can be referenced (resource, module, etc.).
    21→//
    22→// Even if the thing has no name, this should return an empty list. By
    23→// implementing this and returning a non-nil result, you say that this CAN
    24→// be referenced and other methods of referencing may still be possible (such
    25→// as by path!)
    26→type GraphNodeReferenceable interface {
    27→	GraphNodeModulePath
    28→
    29→	// ReferenceableAddrs returns a list of addresses through which this can be
    30→	// referenced.
    31→	ReferenceableAddrs() []addrs.Referenceable
    32→}
    33→
    34→// GraphNodeReferencer must be implemented by nodes that reference other
    35→// Terraform items and therefore depend on them.
    36→type GraphNodeReferencer interface {
    37→	GraphNodeModulePath
    38→
    39→	// References returns a list of references made by this node, which
    40→	// include both a referenced address and source location information for
    41→	// the reference.
    42→	References() []*addrs.Reference
    43→}

    15→//

    17→// represents the state for a particular _instance_, while InstanceState

   138→func (ctx *BuiltinEvalContext) InitProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config *configs.Provider) (providers.Interface, error) {
   139→	// If we already initialized, it is an error
   140→	if p := ctx.Provider(addr); p != nil {
   141→		return nil, fmt.Errorf("%s is already initialized", addr)
   142→	}
   143→
   144→	// Warning: make sure to acquire these locks AFTER the call to Provider
   145→	// above, since it also acquires locks.
   146→	ctx.ProviderLock.Lock()
   147→	defer ctx.ProviderLock.Unlock()
   148→
   149→	key := addr.String()
   150→
   151→	if addr.Module.IsRoot() {
   152→		rootAddr := addrs.RootProviderConfig{
   153→			Provider: addr.Provider,
   154→			Alias:    addr.Alias,
   155→		}
   156→		if external, isExternal := ctx.ExternalProviderConfigs[rootAddr]; isExternal {
   157→			// External providers should always be pre-configured by the
   158→			// external caller, and so we'll wrap them in a type that
   159→			// makes operations like ConfigureProvider and Close be no-op.
   160→			wrapped := externalProviderWrapper{external}
   161→			ctx.ProviderCache[key] = wrapped
   162→			return wrapped, nil
   163→		}
   164→	}
   165→
   166→	p, err := ctx.Plugins.NewProviderInstance(addr.Provider)
   167→	if err != nil {
   168→		return nil, err
   169→	}
   170→
   171→	log.Printf("[TRACE] BuiltinEvalContext: Initialized %q provider for %s", addr.String(), addr)
   172→
   173→	// The config might be nil, if there was no config block defined for this
   174→	// provider.
   175→	if config != nil && config.Mock {
   176→		log.Printf("[TRACE] BuiltinEvalContext: Mocked %q provider for %s", addr.String(), addr)
   177→		p = &providers.Mock{
   178→			Provider: p,
   179→			Data:     config.MockData,
   180→		}

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive investigation of Terraform's plan/apply pipeline architecture. Here's what I've created:

## Summary

I've written a detailed investigation document to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` that answers all four architectural questions about Terraform's planning system:

### **Q1: Command to Context** 
Documents how `PlanCommand.Run()` delegates through the backend to `Context.Plan()`, including the key fields of `PlanOpts` that control plan behavior (Mode, Targets, ForceReplace, SkipRefresh, DeferralAllowed, etc.)

### **Q2: Graph Construction Pipeline**
Details the 13+ sequence of `GraphTransformer` stages that build the dependency graph:
- **ConfigTransformer**: Creates resource nodes from configuration
- **ReferenceTransformer**: Analyzes expressions and adds dependency edges between nodes
- **AttachStateTransformer**: Associates prior state with resource instances
- Plus provider setup, module expansion, and ordering transformers

### **Q3: Provider Resolution and Configuration**
Explains:
- `InitProvider()` instantiates provider plugins via gRPC and caches them
- `ConfigureProvider()` calls the provider's `ConfigureProvider()` RPC with evaluated config
- Provider nodes execute before resources (graph edge ordering)
- `CloseProviderTransformer` adds nodes that close providers after all resources complete

### **Q4: Diff Computation per Resource**
Traces the complete execution path:
1. **Refresh Phase** - `refresh()` calls `provider.ReadResource()` RPC to sync state
2. **Planning Phase** - `plan()` calls `provider.PlanResourceChange()` RPC with prior/proposed state
3. **Action Determination** - `getAction()` determines create/update/replace/delete based on changes
4. **Change Recording** - Results written to plan for apply phase

Plans that contain deferred actions can't converge in\n\t// a single run, and their configuration must be planned again after the\n\t// dependencies of their deferred objects are in a usable state. Various\n\t// events can cause deferrals, including unknown values in count and\n\t// for_each arguments, and deferral notices from providers. Since this is a NoOp we know\n\t\t\t// that the stored dependencies will have no effect during apply, and we can\n\t\t\t// write them out now.\n\t\t\tif change.Action == plans.NoOp && !depsEqual(instanceRefreshState.Dependencies, n.Dependencies) {\n\t\t\t\t// the refresh state will be the final state for this resource, so\n\t\t\t\t// finalize the dependencies here if they need to be updated.\n\t\t\t\tinstanceRefreshState.Dependencies = n.Dependencies\n\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(n.writeResourceInstanceState(ctx, instanceRefreshState, refreshState))\n\t\t\t\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn diags\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Post-conditions might block completion. The following value types may be returned:\n\t//\n\t//   nil + exact true: the node does not require a provider\n\t// * addrs.LocalProviderConfig: the provider was set in the resource config\n\t// * addrs.AbsProviderConfig + exact true: the provider configuration was\n\t//   taken from the instance state.\n\t// * addrs.AbsProviderConfig + exact false: no config or state; the returned\n\t//   value is a default provider configuration address for the resource's\n\t//   Provider\n\tProvidedBy() (addr addrs.ProviderConfig, exact bool)\n\n\t// Provider() returns the Provider FQN for the node.\n\tProvider() (provider addrs.Provider)\n\n\t// Set the resolved provider address for this resource.\n\tSetProvider(addrs.AbsProviderConfig)\n}\n\n// ProviderTransformer is a GraphTransformer that maps resources to providers\n// within the graph. This will error if there are any resources that don't map\n// to proper resources.\ntype ProviderTransformer struct {\n\tConfig *configs.Config\n}\n\nfunc (t *ProviderTransformer) Transform(g *Graph) error {\n\t// We need to find a provider configuration address for each resource\n\t// either directly represented by a node or referenced by a node in\n\t// the graph, and then create graph edges from provider to provider user\n\t// so that the providers will get initialized first.\n\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\t// To start, we'll collect the _requested_ provider addresses for each\n\t// node, which we'll then resolve (handling provider inheritence, etc) in\n\t// the next step.\n\t// Our \"requested\" map is from graph vertices to string representations of\n\t// provider config addresses (for deduping) to requests.\n\ttype ProviderRequest struct {\n\t\tAddr  addrs.AbsProviderConfig\n\t\tExact bool // If true, inheritence from parent modules is not attempted\n\t}\n\trequested := map[dag.Vertex]map[string]ProviderRequest{}\n\tneedConfigured := map[string]addrs.AbsProviderConfig{}\n\tfor _, v := range g.Vertices() {\n\t\t// Does the vertex _directly_ use a provider?\n\t\tif pv, ok := v.(GraphNodeProviderConsumer); ok {\n\t\t\tproviderAddr, exact := pv.ProvidedBy()\n\t\t\tif providerAddr == nil && exact {\n\t\t\t\t// no provider is required\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\trequested[v] = make(map[string]ProviderRequest)\n\n\t\t\tvar absPc addrs.AbsProviderConfig\n\n\t\t\tswitch p := providerAddr.(type) {\n\t\t\tcase addrs.AbsProviderConfig:\n\t\t\t\t// ProvidedBy() returns an AbsProviderConfig when the provider\n\t\t\t\t// configuration is set in state, so we do not need to verify\n\t\t\t\t// the FQN matches.\n\t\t\t\tabsPc = p\n\n\t\t\t\tif exact {\n\t\t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] ProviderTransformer: %s is provided by %s exactly\", dag.VertexName(v), absPc)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tcase addrs.LocalProviderConfig:\n\t\t\t\t// ProvidedBy() return a LocalProviderConfig when the resource\n\t\t\t\t// contains a `provider` attribute\n\t\t\t\tabsPc.Provider = pv.Provider()\n\t\t\t\tmodPath := pv.ModulePath()\n\t\t\t\tif t.Config == nil {\n\t\t\t\t\tabsPc.Module = modPath\n\t\t\t\t\tabsPc.Alias = p.Alias\n\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t\tabsPc.Module = modPath\n\t\t\t\tabsPc.Alias = p.Alias\n\n\t\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t\t// This should never happen; return.\n\tclose(watchStop)\n\t<-watchWait\n\n\treturn walker, diags\n}\n\nfunc (c *Context) graphWalker(graph *Graph, operation walkOperation, opts *graphWalkOpts) *ContextGraphWalker {\n\tvar state states.NewState().SyncWrapper()\n\n\t\t// validate currently uses the plan graph, so we have to populate the\n\t\t// refreshState and the prevRunState.\n\t\trefreshState = states.NewState().SyncWrapper()\n\t\tprevRunState = states.NewState().SyncWrapper()\n\n\tcase walkPlan, walkPlanDestroy, walkImport:\n\t\tstate = inputState.DeepCopy().SyncWrapper()\n\t\trefreshState inputState.DeepCopy().SyncWrapper()\n\t\t// Only plan-like walks use refreshState and prevRunState\n\n\t\t// Discard the input state's check results, because we should create\n\t\t// a new set as a Reference resolution uses langrefs package to parse HCL expressions\n\n**Example Dependencies**:\n- Resource B referencing resource A's output creates edge: B \u2192 A\n- Data source referencing resource attribute creates edge: datasource \u2192 resource\n- Module variable referencing resource creates edge: module_var \u2192 resource\n\n### AttachStateTransformer: State Association\nLocation: `internal/terraform/transform_attach_state.go:29-71`\n\n**Purpose**: Associates stored state with resource instance nodes for refresh/plan\n\n**Mechanism** (lines 35-71):\n1. Q3: Provider Resolution and Configuration\n\n### Overview\nProviders are resolved by the graph builder, initialized during graph walk via EvalContext methods, and configured with provider based on:\n```go\ngetAction(\n    addr,\n    unmarkedPriorVal,        // Prior state\n    unmarkedPlannedNewVal,   // Planned new state\n    createBeforeDestroy,     // CBD configuration\n    forceReplace,            // User force-replace\n    reqRep,                  // RequiresReplace from provider\n)\n```\n\n**Action Determination Logic**:\n1. **No Prior State** (prior == null):\n   - If config present \u2192 **Create**\n   - If config absent \u2192 Skip (no action)\n\n2. **Prior State Exists**:\n   - Compare prior to planned using requiresReplace:\n     - Any attribute in RequiresReplace changes \u2192 **Replace**\n     - Other changes \u2192 **Update**\n     - No changes \u2192 **NoOp**\n\n3. **Force Replace Override**:\n   - If in forceReplace list and action is Update/NoOp:\n     - Force to **Replace** (CreateThenDelete or DeleteThenCreate)\n\n4. **CreateBeforeDestroy Handling**:\n   - If replacing and createBeforeDestroy: **CreateThenDelete**\n   - If replacing and !createBeforeDestroy: **DeleteThenCreate**\n\n5. **Tainted Resource**:\n   - If prior marked tainted: Always **Replace**\n\n**Action Types**:\n- `plans.Create`: Resource doesn't exist, will be created\n- `plans.Update`: Resource exists, will be modified\n- `plans.DeleteThenCreate`: Replace by destroying then creating (default)\n- `plans.CreateThenDelete`: Replace by creating then destroying (CBD)\n- `plans.Delete`: Resource exists, will be destroyed\n- `plans.NoOp`: No changes needed\n- `plans.Forget`: Remove from state without destroying\n\n#### Sensitivity Tracking\n**Lines 1164-1166**: Mark changes in sensitivity as Update\n\n```go\nif action == plans.NoOp && !valueMarksEqual(plannedNewVal, priorVal) {\n    action = plans.Update  // Sensitivity change counts as update\n}\n```\n\n### Change Object Creation\n**Lines 1192-1208**: Package results into plans.ResourceInstanceChange\n\n```go\nplan := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n    Addr:         n.Addr,\n Current state\n        After:  plannedNewVal, // Planned state\n    },\n    ActionReason:    actionReason,\n    RequiredReplace: reqRep,\n}\n```\n\n### State Persistence\n**Lines 1211-1221**: Create planned state object\n\n```go\nstate := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n    Status:  states.ObjectPlanned,  // Marks as incomplete\n    Value:   plannedNewVal,\n    Private: plannedPrivate,\n}\n```\n\n**Key Points**:\n- Status.ObjectPlanned indicates plan-only, not yet applied\n- Expression evaluators prefer plan over planned state\n- Applied plan replaces this with actual state\n\n### Change Recording\n**Line 424** (in managedResourceExecute): `n.writeChange(ctx, change, \"\")`\n- Writes computed change to sync.Changes plan object\n- Accessible for UI display The pipeline is orchestrated by **PlanGraphBuilder**.\n\n### PlanGraphBuilder.Build() and Steps()\nIn `internal/terraform/graph_builder_plan.go:112-277`:\n\n```go\nfunc (b *PlanGraphBuilder) Build(path addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n    return (&BasicGraphBuilder{\n        Steps: b.Steps(),\n        Name:  \"PlanGraphBuilder\",\n    }).Build(path)\n}\n\nfunc (b *PlanGraphBuilder) Steps() []GraphTransformer\n```\n\n#### Sequence of Graph Transformers\nThe `Steps()` method returns an ordered list of transformers that progressively build the graph:\n\n### Phase 1: Core Node Creation\n**Lines 137-146**: Foundational node creation\n- **ConfigTransformer** (line 137-146): Creates resource nodes from configuration\n  - Reference resolution uses langrefs package to parse HCL expressions\n\n**Example Dependencies**:\n- Resource B referencing resource A's output creates edge: B \u2192 A\n- Data source referencing resource attribute creates edge: datasource \u2192 resource\n- Module variable referencing resource creates edge: module_var \u2192 resource\n\n### AttachStateTransformer: State Association\nLocation: `internal/terraform/transform_attach_state.go:29-71`\n\n**Purpose**: Associates stored state with resource instance nodes for refresh/plan\n\n**Mechanism** (lines 35-71):\n1. Q3: Provider Resolution and Configuration\n\n### Overview\nProviders are resolved by the graph builder, initialized during graph walk via EvalContext methods, and configured with provider configuration blocks before resources access them.\n\n### Provider Resolution - ProviderTransformer\nLocation: `internal/terraform/transform_provider.go:90-249`\n\n**Process** (lines 97-249):\n1. For each request:\n   - Resolves provider address considering provider inheritance\n   - Maps to actual provider configuration in module hierarchy\n   - Creates edges from resources to provider nodes\n3. Provider configuration addresses follow inheritance chain up to root module\n\n**Provider Inheritance Mechanism** (lines 189-201):\n- Resources specify providers via local addresses\n- Transformer resolves to absolute provider configuration in ancestor modules\n- If no provider found at current level, walks up module path\n- Respects provider aliases for multiple provider instances\n\n### Provider Initialization via EvalContext\n\n#### InitProvider() Method\nLocation: `internal/terraform/eval_context_builtin.go:138-186`\n\n**Signature**:\n```go\nfunc (ctx *BuiltinEvalContext) Result shows created resource with computed values unknown\n\n#### Action Determination\n**Line 1054**: `action, actionReason := getAction(...)`\n\nThis critical function determines the action type based on:\n```go\ngetAction(\n    addr,\n    unmarkedPriorVal,        // Prior state\n    unmarkedPlannedNewVal,   // Planned new state\n    createBeforeDestroy,     // CBD configuration\n    forceReplace,            // User force-replace\n    reqRep,                  // RequiresReplace from provider\n)\n```\n\n**Action Determination Logic**:\n1. **No Prior State** (prior == null):\n   - If config present \u2192 **Create**\n   - If config absent \u2192 Skip (no action)\n\n2. **Prior State Exists**:\n   - Compare prior to planned using requiresReplace:\n     - Any attribute in RequiresReplace changes \u2192 **Replace**\n     - Other changes \u2192 **Update**\n     - No changes \u2192 **NoOp**\n\n3. **Force Replace Override**:\n   - If in forceReplace list and action is Update/NoOp:\n     - Force to **Replace** (CreateThenDelete or DeleteThenCreate)\n\n4. **CreateBeforeDestroy Handling**:\n   - If replacing and createBeforeDestroy: **CreateThenDelete**\n   - If replacing and !createBeforeDestroy: **DeleteThenCreate**\n\n5. **Tainted Resource**:\n   - If prior marked tainted: Always **Replace**\n\n**Action Types**:\n- `plans.Create`: Resource doesn't exist, will be created\n- `plans.Update`: Resource exists, will be modified\n- `plans.DeleteThenCreate`: Replace by destroying then creating (default)\n- `plans.CreateThenDelete`: Replace by creating then destroying (CBD)\n- `plans.Delete`: Resource exists, will be destroyed\n- `plans.NoOp`: No changes needed\n- `plans.Forget`: Remove from state without destroying\n\n#### Sensitivity Tracking\n**Lines 1164-1166**: Mark changes in sensitivity as Update\n\n```go\nif action == plans.NoOp && !valueMarksEqual(plannedNewVal, priorVal) {\n    action = plans.Update  // Sensitivity change counts as update\n}\n```\n\n### Change Object Creation\n**Lines 1192-1208**: Package results into plans.ResourceInstanceChange\n\n```go\nplan := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n    Addr:         n.Addr,\n    PrevRunAddr:  n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n    Private:      plannedPrivate,\n    ProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n    Change: plans.Change{\n        Action: action,\n        Before: priorVal,      // Current state\n        After:  plannedNewVal, // Planned state\n    },\n    ActionReason:    actionReason,\n    RequiredReplace: reqRep,\n}\n```\n\n### State Persistence\n**Lines 1211-1221**: Create planned state object\n\n```go\nstate := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n    Status:  states.ObjectPlanned,  // Marks as incomplete\n    Value:   plannedNewVal,\n    Private: plannedPrivate,\n}\n```\n\n**Key Points**:\n- Status.ObjectPlanned indicates plan-only, not yet applied\n- Expression evaluators prefer plan over planned state\n- Applied plan replaces this with actual state\n\n### Change Recording\n**Line 424** (in managedResourceExecute): `n.writeChange(ctx, change, \"\")`\n- Writes computed change to sync.Changes plan object\n- Accessible for UI display # Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture

## Q1: Command to Context

### Overview
The CLI plan command delegates to the backend, which creates and invokes the Terraform context's Plan() method. The execution flow is:
1. **PlanCommand.Run()** (internal/command/plan.go:22-118)
2. Delegates to **backend.RunOperation()** with operation request
3. Backend calls **Context.Plan()** (internal/terraform/context_plan.go:155-158)

### Key Components

#### PlanCommand.Run() - CLI Entry Point
Located in `internal/command/plan.go:22-118`:
- Parses command-line flags and arguments
- Calls `c.PrepareBackend()` to load the backend
- Builds operation request with `c.OperationRequest()`
- Calls `c.RunOperation(be, opReq)` to delegate to backend

#### OperationRequest Construction
In `internal/command/plan.go:145-190`, the operation request is built with:
- **Type**: `backendrun.OperationTypePlan`
- **PlanMode**: Normal, Destroy, or RefreshOnly (from args.PlanMode)
- **PlanRefresh**: Whether to refresh state (from args.Refresh)
- **Targets**: Resource targeting addresses (args.Targets)
- **ForceReplace**: Resources to force replacement (args.ForceReplace)
- **Hooks**: Plan view hooks for visualization
- **DeferralAllowed**: Experimental deferral support flag

#### Context.Plan() Method
In `internal/terraform/context_plan.go:155-158`:
```go
func (c *Context) Plan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, tfdiags.Diagnostics)
```
- Delegates to **PlanAndEval()** (internal/terraform/context_plan.go:169-372)

#### Context.PlanAndEval() - Core Planning
In `internal/terraform/context_plan.go:169-372`:
- Validates and normalizes inputs
- Checks external provider configurations
- Routes to operation-specific plan methods based on `opts.Mode`:
  - `plans.
